5. Cultura Viva: Las Farmacias y la AutomedicaciÃ³n en EspaÃ±a

4. GramÃ¡tica Esencial

1. ë™ì‚¬ ê²°í•©ì— ë”°ë¥¸ ì˜ë¯¸ ë³€í™” (Ser vs. Estar + Adjective)

í˜•ìš©ì‚¬ (Adjective) Ser (ë³¸ì§ˆ/ì„±ê²©) Estar (ìƒíƒœ)

2. ì¬ê·€ë™ì‚¬ (Verbos Reflexivos): ê¸°ë¶„ì˜ ë³€í™”

ì£¼ì–´ì˜ í–‰ë™ì´ ë‹¤ì‹œ ì£¼ì–´ ìì‹ ì—ê²Œ ëŒì•„ì˜¤ëŠ” ì¬ê·€ë™ì‚¬ëŠ” 'ê¸°ë¶„ì´ë‚˜ ìƒíƒœì˜ ë³€í™”'ë¥¼ ë‚˜íƒ€ë‚¼ ë•Œ ìì£¼ ì“°ì…ë‹ˆë‹¤.

English Bridge: Reflexive verbs are like saying "I myself feel..." â€” the action reflects back to the subject. English uses "myself/yourself" sparingly, but Spanish uses reflexive pronouns constantly for emotional changes.

ì¬ê·€ëŒ€ëª…ì‚¬: me, te, se, nos, os, se

ì£¼ì–´ (Subject) sentirse (ëŠë¼ë‹¤) ponerse (~ì´ ë˜ë‹¤)
yo me siento me pongo
tÃº te sientes te pones
Ã©l/ella/usted se siente se pone
nosotros/as nos sentimos nos ponemos
vosotros/as os sentÃ­s os ponÃ©is

4. GramÃ¡tica Esencial

A. Gustarí˜• ë™ì‚¬ (Verbs like "Gustar")

ì£¼ì–´ê°€ ì‚¬ëŒì´ ì•„ë‹ˆë¼ 'ì¢‹ì•„í•˜ëŠ” ëŒ€ìƒ'ì´ ë˜ëŠ” íŠ¹ìˆ˜ ë™ì‚¬ë“¤ì…ë‹ˆë‹¤.

English Bridge: English says "I like chocolate" (I = subject). Spanish says "Chocolate pleases me" (Chocolate = subject). This is the reverse construction â€” the thing you like is the grammatical subject!

ì—­í–‰ êµ¬ì¡° (Reverse) ì˜ˆë¬¸ (Example) English Mapping

ğŸ’¡ Key Rule: ëŒ€ìƒì´ ë‹¨ìˆ˜ì´ë©´ gusta, ë³µìˆ˜ì´ë©´ gustan. ë™ì‚¬ ë³€í™”ëŠ” í•­ìƒ ì¢‹ì•„í•˜ëŠ” 'ë¬¼ê±´'ì— ë§ì¶¥ë‹ˆë‹¤. âš ï¸ "Molestar" = to bother/annoy (NOT the English meaning of "molest") â€” False Friend!

B. ë¶€ì •ì–´ì˜ ì‚¬ìš© (La NegaciÃ³n)

ìŠ¤í˜ì¸ì–´ëŠ” ë¶€ì •ì–´ë¥¼ ê°•ì¡°í•˜ê¸° ìœ„í•´ 'ì´ì¤‘ ë¶€ì •'ì„ ìì£¼ ì‚¬ìš©í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤.

English Bridge: English says "I don't eat anything" (single negative). Spanish says "No como nada" (double negative = NOT nothing). In Spanish, double negatives make the negation stronger, not positive!

  • Nada (nothing), Nadie (nobody), Nunca/JamÃ¡s (never)

  • êµ¬ì¡° 2: No como carne nunca. (I don't eat meat ever â€” ë” ì¼ë°˜ì )
